Domestic Important Telegrams

吉黑Combined Army attack on the northwest suburb of Harbin

Harbin heard artillery fire extremely密道 outside the complete shutdown of the market

路轨between Qingshan and Andatar was demolished by the Self-Defense Forces

(Harbin) Ma Zhanshan and Ding Chao Li Du departments, along Huhai East Railway two lines, toward Harbin 急进, Japanese aircraft flew to Xinglong Town and other places侦察this morning, was pursued by Ma Department fighters to escape return, between Qingshan and Andata stations 路道, were demolished by the Self-Defense Forces, the war in the northwest of Harbin is not yet息, (25 special electricity)

Total Market Closure in Daowai, Harbin

(Harbin) Since arriving in Harbin, the situation has suddenly become tense. From the evening of the 23rd, gunshots were very frequent in the northwest of Harbin. This morning, the market in Daowai was completely closed, with puppet police and Japanese soldiers inspecting pedestrians. Many young and strong Chinese civilians were falsely accused of being disguised soldiers of the volunteer army and were arrested and killed. (25th Special Dispatch)

Honjo Shigeru Arrives in Harbin

(Harbin) Japanese Army Commander-in-Chief Honjo Shigeru arrived here today from Shenyang, attracting much attention. Honjo's arrival in Harbin coincided with the news that the Japanese army was rapidly advancing along the eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway and the Songhua River towards the Russian border. The Japanese army is currently undertaking large-scale movements over a wide area. Although Honjo Shigeru has expanded the front lines to the north, northeast, and east of Harbin, in the west, only 25 kilometers from Harbin, the troops of Ma Zhanshan are resisting them. Gunfire was heard in Harbin last night, continuing all night. This morning, several Japanese aircraft took off and flew back and forth over the western section of the Chinese Eastern Railway throughout the day. This morning, a large number of Japanese reinforcements boarded trains and went west to aid the battle. All forms of transportation between Harbin and Qiqihar, except for airplanes, have been cut off. It is reported that Ma Zhanshan's troops have demolished the railway tracks. According to Japanese sources, after the Japanese reinforcements arrive, the Chinese army will gradually retreat, and railway transportation will be restored. However, local people believe that the Japanese news is too optimistic, as they know that Ma Zhanshan still has heavy troops stationed on the western railway line. (24th Reuters Dispatch)

Volunteer Army Plans to Destroy the South Manchuria Railway Tracks

(Beiping) Quan Gusheng, the head of the Huai'de County Public Security Team, led 300 men and joined forces with Wang Delin's troops to destroy the South Manchuria Railway tracks. (25th Special Dispatch)

Volunteer Army Attacks Xingcheng from Suizhong

(Beiping) Three routes of the volunteer army attacked Xingcheng from Suizhong last night and engaged in fierce fighting with the Japanese army, killing more than 30 enemies, wounding more than 70, and seizing more than 200 guns. (25th Special Dispatch)

Yilan Farmers Form Teams to Resist Japan

(Beiping) Farmers in Jilin's Yilan County have formed an anti-Japanese association of about 20,000 people, who have already come into contact with the Japanese. (25th Special Dispatch)

Train Collision Near Yimianpo

(Harbin) It was learned tonight that a train on the eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway, carrying railway employees and their families fleeing the chaotic area, was heading to Harbin. However, there was a Japanese armored train in front of this train, and a freight train behind it. While traveling near Yimianpo, the freight train behind suddenly increased its speed and sped forward, colliding with the passenger train carrying the fleeing railway employees and overturning fourteen passenger cars. The railway employees originally wanted to seek refuge, but now they encountered a disaster. The sounds of crying were unbearable to hear. Fourteen people died on the spot, and thirty-two were seriously injured, many of whom were women and children. It is reported that there are quite a few people who suffered minor injuries, but the number is not yet known in detail. Although the accident site was near Yimianpo, the injured only received initial treatment because the Yimianpo hospital was full of wounded soldiers and had no space available. Therefore, the injured were all placed in the other two trains and transported to Harbin. (24th Reuters Dispatch)

Ma Zhanshan's Troops Telegraph Victory

(Nanjing) Jiao and Wu, two regiments of Ma Zhanshan's troops, telegraphed to the capital, stating that when they were ordered to coordinate with the troops of Ding and Li to attack Harbin, the Japanese army bypassed their rear and invaded Tonghe, causing great devastation. Upon hearing this, their regiments led troops back to aid, deployed in the suburbs, and took advantage of the enemy's complacency at night to launch a sudden encirclement and fierce attack, killing countless enemies and seizing a large amount of weapons and ammunition. They are currently pursuing the enemy. (25th Central News Agency Dispatch)

The Process of Japanese Nationals Withdrawing from Tonghua

(Beiping) Some time ago, the Japanese side sent Nishida with an official document from the Shenyang Consul-General to apologize to the 10th Route of the Self-Defense Army stationed in Tonghua, requesting the consular officials and residents stationed in Tonghua to leave, and acknowledging: (1) The Japanese army will withdraw from Tonghua and will not take military action. (2) The Japanese soldiers' protection of the consuls and residents going to Tonghua was voluntary. (3) If the Japanese soldiers commit any further offenses, the Japanese side is at fault, and the true situation can be reported to the international community. On May 9th, the Japanese side used forty-two large vehicles to escort the fifty-four consular staff and residents and two hundred seventy-six Korean residents to their destination and handed them over to the Japanese police, who issued a safety and integrity certificate. (24th Special Dispatch)

Yu Zhishan's Troops Agree to Revolt

(Beiping) Yu Zhishan's troops, numbering over 5,000 in the areas of Liaozhong, Liaoyang, and Tai'an, recently agreed to revolt and plan to concentrate at Liu'erb fort to attack the Japanese. (25th Special Dispatch)

A British Man, Matsuura, Wounded by Gunfire

(Beiping) Regarding the rumor that one British and one American were killed near Harbin, a foreign official telegram states that there were no American casualties. However, a British man named Matsuura, residing near Harbin, was beaten by soldiers of the "Manchukuo" army several days ago, who then opened fire on him, but he did not sustain fatal injuries. (25th Reuters Dispatch)

The Puppet State Bans Laborers from Entering

(Beiping) The puppet state's Ministry of Civil Affairs issued an order to ban laborers from entering. (25th Special Dispatch)

Guangxi Army Enters Guangdong in Two Routes

The Northern Route Has Reached Huaiji, the Southern Route Has Reached Linbin

Air Force Officers and Soldiers Issue a Joint Statement Expressing Solidarity

Chen Ce Increases the Number of Marine Corps Units in Hainan by Thirteen Regiments

(Hong Kong) The Guangxi bandit suppression army entered Guangdong in two routes. One route, from Huaiji, follows Guangning, Sihui, and reaches Sanshui River mouth, where it turns to the North River to meet the northern route troops. The other route starts from Cenxi, passes through Luoding to Liangyang in the south, and meets the southern route troops. One route has already reached Huaiji, and the other route has also reached Linbin in Yunan. The navigation administration branch office established by Guangdong in Yunan, as well as various tax collection agencies, have moved away. Merchants in the West River, fearing the impact of the Guangxi army's eastward advance to suppress bandits, have mostly stopped trading. (25th Special Dispatch)

Air Force Officers and Soldiers Express Solidarity

(Hong Kong) The air force officers and soldiers of Guangdong issued a joint statement on the 25th, stating that to quickly suppress the widespread bandits and communists, there must be a unified military command to achieve coordinated action. This reorganization was ordered entirely to facilitate command and control and has no other intention. Furthermore, there has been no internal disruption of the air force. The rumors circulating outside are completely inconsistent with the facts. We soldiers only know to unite and act consistently, taking obedience to orders as our duty. (25th Special Dispatch)

Chen Jitang Persuades Various Warships to Return

(Hong Kong) Chen Jitang ordered Zhao Guizhang to persuade the large warships Zhongshan, Flying Eagle, and Fuan to return, offering a reward of 200,000 yuan per ship. Small warships such as Jiangda and eight others will also be heavily rewarded if they return. The captains of each ship are allowed to continue in their positions. (25th Special Dispatch)

Hu Hanmin's Mediation Ends Without Result

(Hong Kong) Hu Hanmin continued to mediate the naval unrest for several days, but Chen Ce's attitude was firm, and he has given up hope. Hu has relinquished responsibility for mediation and has returned it to the free handling of one group. (25th Dispatch)

Wu Chaochu Mediates Naval Unrest

(Hong Kong) Wu Chaochu came to Hong Kong on the 24th to mediate the naval unrest. There was no news as of the 25th. (25th Special Dispatch)

Chen Ce's Troops Seize Weapons from Self-Defense Corps

(Hong Kong) Chen Ce's troops in Hainan seized tens of thousands of weapons from the self-defense corps and increased the number of marine corps units by thirteen regiments. (25th Special Dispatch)

Lin Yungai to Assume Position as Director Tomorrow

(Hong Kong) Lin Yungai is scheduled to assume the concurrent position of Director of Construction on the 27th. (25th Special Dispatch)

Zhang Zhiying Leads Troops to the Southern Route

(Hong Kong) Zhang Zhiying led two regiments of troops on the 24th and departed from Huangpu by ship to the southern route. (25th Special Dispatch)

Central Committee Members Staying in Guangdong to Issue Joint Statement

(Hong Kong) The Guangdong Central Committee will issue a joint statement in response to Yu's impeachment proposal against Wang. The draft can be completed on the 26th. (25th Special Dispatch)

19th Route Army Prepares to Leave Nanjing for Fujian

5th Army Takes Over Defense of the Nanjing-Shanghai Line

Overseas Chinese Volunteer Army Decides to Withdraw

(Nanjing) The 19th Route Army has been ordered to leave for Fujian to suppress bandits. The General Command for Bandit Suppression has issued orders to its subordinates to prepare to depart after the 28th. The Nanjing-Shanghai line will be taken over by the 5th Army. (25th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) As the 19th Route Army is about to leave for Fujian to suppress bandits, the Overseas Chinese Volunteer Army has requested and been granted permission by Commander Mao to withdraw in order to go north to resist Japan. Commander Mao will hold a farewell ceremony on the 30th and present them with an anti-Japanese commemorative medal. The army has also petitioned the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission for spiritual and material assistance. (25th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The 61st Division of the 19th Army stationed in Nanjing has today complied with the order of the Military Affairs Commission to depart for Fujian. The troops of this army stationed along the Nanjing-Shanghai line will also depart for Fujian soon. (25th Reuters Dispatch)

Cai Tingkai Recruits New Soldiers in Guangdong

(Hong Kong) Cai Tingkai telegraphed Tan Qixiu, stating that he will recruit new troops in Guangdong and reorganize them into four regiments, which will depart to rejoin the main force in a short period. (25th Special Dispatch)

Guangdong Political Council Plans to Subsidize Military Expenses Monthly

(Hong Kong) The Political Council plans to subsidize the 19th Route Army's expenses with 200,000 yuan per month. (25th Special Dispatch)

Ou Shounian and Weng Zhaoyuan Arrive in Changzhou

(Changzhou) Ou Shounian, commander of the 78th Division of the 19th Route Army, arrived in Changzhou today from Nanjing. Weng Zhaoyuan, commander of the 156th Brigade under his command, also came to Changzhou from Wuxi. Commander Ou gathered his troops at the sports field to give a speech, while Brigade Commander Weng returned to Wuxi that evening. In the evening, various organizations hosted a banquet for Commander Ou at the Chamber of Commerce. (25th Special Dispatch)

Fujian Provincial Defense Committee

To Be Chaired by Liu Heding

(Fuzhou) This morning's joint meeting of the Party, government, and military appointed Liu Heding as the chairman of the Provincial Defense Committee. (24th Dispatch)

Guangdong Army Entering Jiangxi First Plans to Consolidate Guangdong Border

Talks with Chen Jitang's Representative

(Nanchang) Li Shangyong, representative of Chen Jitang, said, "When I was still in Dayu on the 21st, Li's division decided not to leave Ganzhou. Those entering Jiangxi must first clear the area south of Ganzhou, including Chongyou, Yudu, Xinfeng, Nankang, and the Three Nan Counties, to consolidate the Guangdong border before advancing towards Xingyu. Those entering Fujian will wait until 20 divisions have been added and the central government's maritime forces arrive in Fujian before launching a joint attack. After recovering the Guangdong navy and air force, 400,000 yuan will be saved monthly." (24th Special Dispatch)

Peng's Bandits Flee Towards Shangyou

Zhao and Shangguan's Troops Will Return to Civil Life

Japanese Marines Conduct Street Fighting Drills in Yuguan

Lytton and Others Organize Investigative Documents

No Knowledge from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Regarding Trusteeship

(Shenyang) Five experts from the investigation team, after completing their inspection of Qiqihar, returned to Shenyang at 00:05 today via the Siping-Taonan Railway. (25th Dentsu Dispatch)

Southwest Association for Foreign Affairs Opposes Ceasefire Agreement

(Hong Kong) The Southwest Association for Foreign Affairs issued a joint statement on the 23rd, opposing the ceasefire agreement. It also stated that the government has recently transferred elite troops and concentrated them in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, neither defending against foreign aggression nor suppressing the communists. What is the purpose? If this leads to internal strife, it is feared that the country will perish more quickly. It is hoped that the government will make a firm decision to resist Japan. Otherwise, if it does not confront foreign enemies but instead turns inward, it will willingly become a public enemy of the people and be abandoned by the entire nation. (25th Special Dispatch)

Tianjin and Beiping Municipal Governments Plan to Establish Temporary Postal Delivery Offices

Japanese Residents in Tianjin Plan to Operate Their Own Post Office

(Tianjin) The Municipal Government plans to establish temporary postal delivery offices and has reached an agreement with the Beiping Municipal Government to jointly operate them. Starting from the 27th, mail will be collected and delivered. Mail to Beiping and Shanghai will be sent by train under military escort. (25th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The British Chamber of Commerce sent representatives on the 25th to visit Section Chief Corden of the Customs to request that mail from the British to Tianjin be checked and released. Corden replied that it had been locked in the warehouse and could not be checked. (25th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The municipal governments of Beiping and Tianjin, in order to remedy the inconvenience caused by the postal workers' strike, are planning to establish postal delivery offices. In all places along the railway line, personnel will be sent to the stations, and the local authorities will dispatch police to deliver the mail yesterday. In this city, bicycle teams will be used for delivery. The Tianjin Municipal Government and the Social Affairs Bureau have begun to handle the matter. It will be canceled when the postal workers return to work. If the return to work is indefinite or the organization expands... (25th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Based on the demands of Japanese residents, the Japanese Consulate sent personnel to the Asahi Street Post Office on the 24th to express to Xu Shaoming that the postal strike has caused great losses to Japanese merchants. If work does not resume within a few days, Japanese residents will operate their own post office. Xu did not reply, only reporting to the labor union. However, the Japanese Resident Corps held a meeting on the 25th to discuss operating their own post office, and their attitude was quite active. (25th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) For the convenience of both Chinese and foreign people, the municipal government has decided to set up a temporary postal delivery office, with Section Chief Xian Daohou of the Third Section and Deng Qinglan, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, responsible for the preparations. The location will be temporarily at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Messengers will be borrowed from the Public Security Bureau's bicycle team. Postal workers are welcome to help. It will be implemented first in this city, and then cooperate with other cities and counties. It will be canceled when postal services resume. According to Mu, it can be implemented on the 26th or 27th. (25th Special Dispatch)

Wang Zhaoming Cables All Provinces and Cities to Do Their Best to Maintain Postal Services

(Nanjing) Wang Zhaoming, President of the Executive Yuan, urgently cabled all provincial and municipal governments and forwarded to county governments on the 25th, stating, "Upon investigation, the various demands of the Shanghai postal workers regarding the treatment of postal workers have been considered and accommodated by the Ministry. As for the merging of the Postal Savings Bureau and the suspension of airmail funding, which relate to national administration and transportation construction, they should be discussed in the long term and cannot be resolved by the Ministry. It is deeply feared that postal workers in various places do not understand this and will take actions outside the scope of their duties. The following measures should be taken immediately: (1) If there are signs of a strike by workers in various places, please first give them sincere persuasion. All employees who have served in the postal service for a certain number of years should be diligently persuaded to listen and work hard. The Executive Yuan will order the Ministry to promote them preferentially as a reward. (2) If a strike has already taken place, an order should be issued to resume work within 24 hours. Those who exceed the time limit will be dismissed. The local telegraph bureau, chamber of commerce, public security bureau, or equivalent agencies should jointly dispatch personnel to assist the local postmaster in organizing a temporary mail collection and delivery agency. Proper arrangements should be made for the dismissal of postal workers to avoid disruption. If there are illegal actions affecting public order, please deal with them strictly. (3) If the postmaster evades responsibility, please instruct the president of the chamber of commerce to preside over the bureau's affairs. (4) The original postage stamps of the post office should be ordered to be handed over. If they are insufficient, proper alternative methods should be devised to avoid abuse. This matter concerns public transportation, and the governments must provide enthusiastic assistance to ensure that the situation is resolved without incident. Please report at any time. This is of utmost importance." (25th Special Dispatch)

Foreign News Briefs

US Congress Discusses Blount Proposal

Advocates Establishment of Dictatorial Government in Honolulu

To Prevent Military Conspiracy by Japanese Americans

National News Agency, Washington, 24th: The US Congress today began handling the Blount proposal, which seeks to establish a military dictatorship in Hawaii. Blount explained that the proposal is necessary for the proper management of Hawaii and is a crucial step to prevent Japanese Americans on the island from conspiring to destroy our military installations overnight in times of emergency. He also cited the recent Massie Case as evidence of the erosion of authority. Rear Admiral Byrd, Commander of the US Navy, stated that he personally had no reason to doubt the loyalty of any American citizens to the country. General MacArthur, Chief of Staff of the Army, also stated that the proposed change in the political system would have little impact on the defense of Hawaii, as the defense of the island must depend on whether there is sufficient naval and military power.

Page 8

After Much Delay

Japanese Elder Cabinet Formed

Prime Minister Saitō Concurrently Serves as Foreign Minister for the Time Being

Inauguration Ceremony Scheduled for Today

China United News Agency, Tokyo, 25th: The Saitō Cabinet was temporarily expected to be stranded due to Tatsuo Yamamoto's firm refusal to serve as Minister of the Interior. However, after persuasion from the leaders of the Minseitō (Constitutional Democratic Party) and Saitō, Yamamoto agreed to join the cabinet. Chief Prosecutor Matsukichi Oyama also accepted the invitation to join the cabinet as Minister of Justice in the afternoon. As Koki Hirota firmly declined to serve as Foreign Minister, Saitō will temporarily serve concurrently. The Foreign Minister post will be filled later by choosing one of two candidates: Ambassador Matsudaira and Keijirō Matsui. Count Kodama will serve as Governor-General of Taiwan. The decision was reported to Saionji at 8:20 PM. The final list of cabinet members is as follows:

Prime Minister and Foreign Minister: Saitō Makoto (75 years old), Minister of Interior: Yamamoto Tatsuo (77 years old), Minister of Finance: Takahashi Korekiyo (79 years old), Minister of the Army: Hayashi Senjūrō (59 years old), Minister of the Navy: Okada Keisuke (65 years old), Minister of Justice: Oyama Matsukichi (64 years old), Minister of Education: Hatoyama Ichirō (50 years old), Minister of Agriculture and Forestry: Gotō Fumio (49 years old), Minister of Commerce and Industry: Nakajima Kumakichi (62 years old), Minister of Railways: Mitsuchi Chūzō (62 years old), Minister of Communications: Minami Hiroshi (64 years old), Minister of Colonial Affairs: Nagai Ryūtarō (52 years old), Chief Cabinet Secretary: Shibata Zensaburō (55 years old), Director-General of the Legislation Bureau: Horikiri Zennosuke (49 years old), Governor-General of Taiwan: Kodama Hideo.

Saitō will present the list of cabinet members to the Emperor for approval tomorrow. Therefore, the inauguration ceremony for the new cabinet members is scheduled for 2:00 PM tomorrow (the 26th).

Far East News Agency, Tokyo, 25th: Since being ordered to form a cabinet, the new Japanese Prime Minister, Saitō, has been very careful, especially considering the current international situation. The position of Foreign Minister is of utmost importance. Saitō considered potential successors and telegraphed Uchida Kōsai, the current President of the South Manchuria Railway, inviting him to join the cabinet as Foreign Minister. President Uchida declined, stating that he was not capable of undertaking such a heavy responsibility and that the South Manchuria Railway was currently expanding various projects, making it difficult for him to leave. He sent a telegram to Saitō this afternoon, declining the offer. Therefore, the position of Foreign Minister has been temporarily decided to be concurrently held by the Prime Minister. In the future, Baron Tsuneo Matsudaira, the Ambassador to Great Britain, is being considered as a successor. Minister of the Interior Yamamoto Tatsuo is an elder statesman of the Minseitō, and is held in high regard within the party. He himself was quite modest about the position of Minister of the Interior. However, after Wakatsuki, the president of Minseitō, and dozens of young members of the party, who desired that Yamamoto come forward, gathered at Yamamoto's private residence this afternoon and urged him strongly, Yamamoto formally replied to Saitō at 6:30 PM, accepting the cabinet position. Admiral Okada, the Minister of the Navy, is a veteran of the naval community, and has long been considered the most suitable candidate for the next Minister of the Navy. Hatoyama Ichirō will remain as Minister of Education. Hatoyama is a key figure in the Suzuki faction of the Seiyūkai (Friends of Constitutional Government Association), and is one of the "three musketeers" of the Suzuki faction. His mother, Haruko, is an elder stateswoman in the education community, and he owes much of his prominence in the education community to his mother's assistance. Mitsuchi, the Minister of Railways, is known as the financial expert of the Seiyūkai, and is a protégé of Takahashi. He served as Minister of Education in the Tanaka cabinet in 1927 and as Minister of Communications in the Inukai cabinet. Oyama, the Minister of Justice, is a giant in the legal community and is currently the Chief Prosecutor. Nagai, the Minister of Colonial Affairs, is currently the Secretary-General of the Minseitō, and served as Parliamentary Vice-Minister for Foreign Affairs in the Inukai cabinet. He is known as an eloquent speaker. Nakajima, the Minister of Commerce and Industry, is a businessman and a member of the Kōseikai (Fair Politics Association) in the House of Peers. Takahashi, the Minister of Finance, was the Minister of Finance in the Inukai cabinet. After Inukai's death, he temporarily served as Prime Minister. He is an elder statesman in the Seiyūkai and the oldest financial expert in Japan. He has served as President of the Bank of Japan, President of Yokohama Specie Bank, Prime Minister in 1921, and has also served as Minister of Agriculture and Commerce and four terms as Minister of Finance. He is now rejoining the cabinet to take charge of the treasury. Gotō, the Minister of Agriculture and Forestry, is a member of the House of Peers and has served as Chief of General Affairs of the Taiwan Governor-General's Office. Minami, the Minister of Communications, is a member of the House of Peers and has served as Vice-Minister of Education. He was appointed Governor-General of Taiwan this year. General Hayashi, the Minister of the Army, is currently the Commander of the Korean Army. In 1923, he attended the League of Nations as the Japanese Army representative. He has also served as Commander of the Tokyo Bay Fortress, President of the Army War College, and Director of the Education Directorate. In 1929, he served as Commander of the Konoe Division. He is a powerful general in the army. In total, the cabinet consists of eleven members, excluding the Foreign Minister, who is concurrently held by the Prime Minister. Four members belong to the Seiyūkai, two belong to the Minseitō, three belong to the House of Peers, and one each belongs to the Army and Navy.

Reuters, Tokyo, 25th: The new government's foreign policy will largely be the same as that of the Seiyūkai government, so it makes no difference who is in charge of foreign affairs.

Important Political Meeting at French Presidential Palace

Herriot Temporarily in Charge of Cabinet Affairs

New Government to be Formed Next Month

Reuters, Paris, 24th: An important political meeting was held at the Presidential Palace this afternoon. Prime Minister Tardieu, Finance Minister Flandin, and other cabinet members were present, and Édouard Herriot, leader of the Radical Socialist Party, also attended. There was a lengthy discussion on foreign affairs and domestic finances. Herriot's new cabinet cannot be formed until the National Assembly convenes, so Tardieu will continue to hold office temporarily, but without authority. France's budget deficit is very large, and the trade balance is increasingly out of balance, so financial issues are currently the most important events in French politics. The new government may be formed by the end of the first week of June, and the Lausanne reparations conference will open on June 16, so the new government will only have one week to seek the confidence of the National Assembly before sending representatives to Lausanne. It is expected that Herriot's cabinet members will mostly be members of the Radical Party, and will include representatives from the Painlevé and Left Center parties. This is because the Socialist Party is demanding a reduction in military spending, the nationalization of insurance, and the creation of poor relief funds as conditions for joining the new cabinet. It is reported that Herriot is unwilling to proceed so abruptly, and has turned to the Painlevé and Left Center parties for their support, in order to gain a majority in the National Assembly.

National News Agency, Paris, 24th: Edouard Herriot, leader of the Radical Party, has today temporarily taken charge of French cabinet affairs. However, this is an informal assumption of office, and Herriot may specialize in the position of Minister of Foreign Affairs without forming a new cabinet himself. Today's informal ceremony was held at the Presidential Palace.

Turmoil in the Prussian Parliament

Polar Opposites Trade Insults

Early Signs of Future Political Upheaval

National News Agency, Berlin, 24th: Since the election of the new Prussian parliament, it has been widely expected to be a new center of upheaval in German domestic politics. As expected, only half an hour after the inaugural meeting was held today, disturbances occurred several times in a row, as if foreshadowing a major future turmoil. The German people, aware of this, are paying close attention to the new parliament. The gallery was already packed before the meeting began. Of course, the eyes of the attendees were all focused on the seats of the National Socialist Party. However, at the beginning, not a single one was present in the party seats. It was not until the meeting was about to begin that 162 deputies entered the chamber in formation. At that moment, cheers of welcome and jeers from the left wing made noise at the same time. Prince Wilhelm, the fourth son of the deposed German Emperor, who has always been known as a stalwart of the National Socialist movement, was especially the target of attack by the communist deputies. Today's inaugural meeting of the new parliament was chaired by General Litzmann, a highly respected member of the National Socialist Party, who is 84 years old. A famous general of the Eastern European battlefield. As soon as the opening ceremony was over, the Communist Party immediately launched an offensive, proposing a motion of no confidence in Chancellor Braun, the acting Prime Minister of Prussia. They also demanded that the parliament immediately discuss the issue of unemployment relief. However, both motions were rejected on procedural grounds, as the parliament decided that it must first elect the speaker, deputy speaker, and other officers before it could proceed with the agenda. At that time, the Communist Party and the National Socialist Party engaged in fierce debates, mutually accusing each other of deceiving the unemployed. After the two motions were rejected, the Communist Party deputies stated that they would still propose the same motion tomorrow. The National Socialist Party also stated that the party had already prepared a similar motion, which would be continued tomorrow when the speaker, deputy speaker, and other officials are elected.

German Foreign Affairs Committee Passes Resolution

Geneva Conference Will be Affected

Important News: Osaka Mainichi Shimbun on the Perilous State of Japanese-American War Machines

(Continuation 3)

After the outbreak of the "Manchurian Crisis," as the Americans called it, in September of last year, I paid close attention to the actions of the United States. At that time, I discovered an unexpected phenomenon, namely, the United States announced its strange opinions at this time. At that time, China sought help from the League of Nations, and the United States, standing outside the League of Nations and acting independently, declared that it would cooperate with the League of Nations. At the same time, it joined the League of Nations, and consistently used an attitude of oppressing Japan to comment on the Manchurian issue. However, clear-headed American diplomats did not find the attitude of the American government to be strange. From the time of President Cleveland to the time of McKinley, in order to protect its own interests and implement its own claims, the United States often used strong-arm tactics abroad. For example, during the heyday of the British Empire, US Secretary of State Olney intervened in the Caribbean Sea issue. When he met with British Foreign Secretary Salisbury, his arrogance was as if there was no one else present. As a result, he was ultimately unable to subdue the other party. This is one example.

When the Manchurian Incident broke out, Stimson's diplomacy towards Japan, self-consciously standing in the position of a great power, upheld its own traditional position and submitted a note to Japan. However, the content of the note was in the nature of a letter of recommendation. For if Japan and the United States separated the buffer zone of the so-called League of Nations and handled the Manchurian Incident separately, a head-on collision would inevitably occur. Therefore, the United States government and other politicians mostly expressed a lukewarm attitude. In particular, the arguments in the American press originally represented the aspirations of the entire United States. After the Manchurian Incident, public opinion towards Japan was very inconsistent. Like the Manchester Guardian in England, which insulted Japan with abusive language and excluded Japan, were still rare. Among them, only the New York Evening Post and the New York World News were relatively intense. When they heard of the Manchurian Incident, they immediately discredited Japan as a barbaric country. The actions of the Japanese army were completely similar to the actions of barbarians, and even bitterly scolded the Japanese militarist policy of aggression. But there were also several newspapers on the other side that vigorously defended Japan. Later, when the issue of economic sanctions arose, it was generally believed in the country that "economic sanctions against a powerful country would induce a world war." The New York News also had two factions on this issue, one advocating it and one opposing it. As public opinion was not unified, the government's policy was difficult to decide. Now, from my personal point of view, observing the situation in the United States and guessing the true intentions of the United States government, there is a big gap between them. Why? Listening to its statements and reading its notes, although they seemed to strongly pretend to be very calm and moderate in tone, their bones actually contained the meaning of oppression, and words of dissatisfaction overflowed. And the tone often used by Secretary of State Stimson really opened up a new and strange precedent in American diplomatic documents. For its arrogant and disrespectful words and deeds, it wanted to oppress the world with its towering power, conceal its own essential nature, and exert a surprising self-control, which was obviously impossible to conceal.

Looking back at October of last year, on American Navy Day, the chairman of the Senate Naval Committee gave a speech on the current situation of the three major naval powers, Britain, the United States, and Japan, and compared the existing power of the navies of the United States and Japan, saying that Japan's naval power was stronger than that of the United States. At the same time, he discussed the current Manchurian Incident, attacking and criticizing Japan's Manchurian policy with all his might. Among them, there were words such as "because the current naval power of the United States cannot control Japan's actions, it is necessary to recover them." From this, we can know that the United States today still dares not actively interfere in Japan's actions. If it wants to interfere in Japan's actions, it has to cause a war. If it wants war, it must not have a superior naval power, and if it wants to prepare a superior navy, it cannot be done in one or two months. This is why the United States is bluffing and only making threatening gestures. Stimson, however, does not understand the situation and incites provocation. It is not worth the laugh of connoisseurs.

Plan to Convert Hangzhou Mint into Arsenal Abandoned

Hangzhou Correspondence: Due to the Shanghai Incident, our army withdrew from Longhua. The military department had transported parts of the arsenal's machinery to Zhejiang, and planned to move the factory to Hangzhou. Wang Zuyao, chairman of the Hangzhou Chamber of Commerce, sent a letter to Chen Yi, Vice Minister of Military Affairs, requesting that this plan be abandoned. Yesterday, he received a reply from Chen, saying that the plan had been abandoned. The exchange of letters is recorded as follows: (1) Wang's letter to Chen Yi said, "Recently, Mr. Guo, the director of the arsenal, brought foreign technicians to Hangzhou to inspect the Hangzhou Mint. It is said that it is planned to convert it into a part of the arsenal. The merchants and residents here are quite alarmed and have come to inquire. Upon investigation, the Hangzhou Mint is located on West Avenue, the provincial capital, and is densely populated. It is also adjacent to a girls' middle school and is very close to the New Market. It is not appropriate to build a dangerous arsenal in a prosperous urban area. I hope that you will care for your hometown and resolutely request that this plan be abandoned. In addition to the city chamber of commerce submitting a request to Chairman Lu of the Zhejiang Provincial Government to telegraph your department, I urge you to strongly preside over the matter, hoping to cancel this move before it is done." (2) Chen Yi's reply to Wang's letter said, "The plan to convert the mint into an arsenal has now been abandoned. I hereby inform you of this, so as to relieve your concerns." (25th)

Local Correspondence Songjiang

Suspects in Qibao Robbery Case Apprehended

Three suspects in the robbery case at the home of Zhang Busheng in Yu Lane, Qibao, namely Du Youyu, Wei Amei, and others, have been apprehended one after another and transferred to the county court for prosecution. According to their confessions, Zhang Atu and Zhang Agen were arrested yesterday by the 14th Sub-Precinct of the Public Security Bureau. After preliminary interrogation by Section Chief Gu, the suspects confessed to the robbery without hesitation. They have been recorded, and their cases have been transferred to the county court for investigation and handling.

Garrisoning of Xuantan Military Police in Songjiang

The 6th Regiment of Military Police garrisoning Danyang and Jurong have been ordered to transfer to Songjiang. The regiment first sent personnel to Songjiang to contact the Public Security Bureau to arrange for the garrison locations. They have determined that Xilin Temple, Guanghua Temple, Fu'an, Chenggong Shrine, and Shiying Nunnery will be used as garrison locations. The troops will arrive in Songjiang today (25th).

Fengjing Station Master Injured in Rescue Attempt

Yesterday (24th), at approximately 2:00 PM, the 33rd Special Express Train from Hangzhou to Shanghai was passing through Fengjing Station. Station Master Yang Qiyuan was performing his duties when the train sped past. Suddenly, four passengers in uniform jumped from the train. The station master tried to stop them, but they refused and jumped down, crashing into the station master. The station master took the brunt of the impact and broke his leg. He lost consciousness and is now being treated at Jiaxing Hospital.

Suzhou Industries Assist Postal Workers' Strike

After receiving news of the Shanghai postal workers' strike, the local postal workers' union immediately telegraphed the Ministry of Communications, requesting the adoption of the postal workers' union's proposal to consolidate the postal base. The banking and other 23 trade associations also believe that this matter is of great importance to commercial transportation, and jointly sent a letter to the county chamber of commerce. On the 23rd, they telegraphed the Ministry of Communications to provide assistance in order to avoid escalating the situation.

5th Army Ordered to Depart

The 88th and 87th Divisions of the 5th Army, which participated in the Shanghai anti-Japanese war, have been stationed in Changshu and Wuxian counties since the end of the war. They have now been ordered to depart. The brigades and regiments of the 88th Division departed for Nanjing on the 22nd and will transfer to Hankou. The brigades and regiments of the 87th Division have been concentrated in Suzhou and are scheduled to depart for Nanjing on the 24th.

Wuxi Jiangsu Province to Impose Special Business Tax

The financial situation of the Jiangsu Provincial Government remains difficult, and the collection of business taxes has not improved. Therefore, following the example of Hubei and other provinces, a special business tax will be implemented. The scope of collection will be based on eight categories: bamboo and wood, paper, cotton, silk cocoons, north-south goods, coal, beans, and oil. The tax rate will be 20 per thousand of the price. Tax bureaus will be established at major ports to collect the tax. The original business tax will be changed to a business license tax. The regulations are currently being drafted and are scheduled to take effect on July 1st. According to Chairman Gu, the special business tax will only be collected once and will not be collected repeatedly. Therefore, it is different from the collection of arrearage fees, and it is also different from the ordinary business tax. It is defined as the whole number of the tax to be levied first, rather than the odd numbers to be levied after the business.

Robberies Occur in City and Countryside

Ding Zixiu, a 63-year-old resident of Changan Bridge Heng Street outside the North Gate, has a modest family fortune and lives comfortably. Suddenly, at approximately 2:00 AM yesterday (25th), five bandits arrived, wearing short clothes and carrying bayonets, bamboo poles, and other items. They first went to Zixiu's room, where two bandits dragged his wife, Mrs. Lu (56 years old), out of bed, tied her up with strips of cloth torn from a bed sheet, and then tied Zixiu up on the bed. The remaining three bandits then rummaged through boxes and chests, looting for approximately two hours before fleeing with their loot. When the bandits were about to leave, they stabbed Zixiu twice in the neck with a bayonet, causing the wounds to pass through both sides. Blood flowed profusely, and he lost consciousness. Afterward, his family members carried the injured person to Puren Hospital for treatment. Also, the homes of Lu Jubao and Lu Hebao, residents of Funan Township in the 9th District of the county, were robbed by more than ten bandits the night before last, who stole six or seven piculs of rice, more than ten items of clothing, and silver dollars, with an estimated loss of more than two hundred yuan. Also, the home of Zheng Aihe in Zhengjiatang in the same district was robbed of clothing, silver dollars, and other items at approximately 10:00 PM on the 21st, with losses estimated at more than one hundred yuan. The 10th Bureau of the Public Security Bureau has arrested four suspects, Hu Agui, Zou Arong, Wu Haoquan, and Chen Jingen, who are currently under investigation.

Labor Dispute at Houch Sheng Silk Factory

The Housheng Silk Factory, located at Nancangmen outside the East Gate, was founded by Mr. Jun Chongli with invested capital. It has 208 Italian-style silk reeling machines. Due to the tragic decline in the silk market, it suffered from poor capital turnover and was forced to declare a shutdown in October of last year. As the fresh silkworm cocoons are about to enter the market, in order to maintain the livelihood of the workers, it is planned to find ways to resume production. Manager Feng Meisheng, Zhang Yongqing, and others consulted to select female workers, and created 208 admission cards, ordering car manager Jiang Jianming to distribute them to the female workers. New female workers account for four-tenths of the total, and old female workers account for six-tenths, which aroused dissatisfaction among the old female workers who did not receive admission cards. Yesterday (24th) morning at 5:00 AM was the date for the factory to resume work. Manager Dan feared an accident and entrusted Wu Liansheng and Ding Zhaochu, two staff members of the silk factory trade union, to monitor the factory gate and collect admission cards. At the time, there were more than 200 female workers at the gate, and their momentum was fierce, intending to disturb the factory. Seeing this, Wu and Ding stepped forward to persuade them, but the female workers beat Wu and Ding severely, and then destroyed all the doors, windows, and walls. Seeing the poor situation, the factory immediately closed the factory gate and reported to the 1st Police Station of the 2nd Branch of the Public Security Bureau by telephone. After receiving the report, the police station immediately sent a patrolman to suppress the situation. At the same time, the police brigade also received the news and rushed to the scene, but the female workers had already dispersed and their whereabouts were unknown. Afterwards, the Silk Adjustment Committee sent representatives Ji Xiansan to the county government to report the situation to County Chief Chen and request the arrest of the leading perpetrators. County Chief Chen was furious upon receiving the report and immediately issued a handwritten order to the Public Security Bureau to send police to investigate and arrest them. It is reported that Wu Guangtao, the ringleader, has been apprehended and taken to the bureau for interrogation. The Housheng Silk Factory has now been postponed to the 28th to resume work.

News After Changzhou Postal Workers' Strike

In order to support the postal foundation plan, postal workers in Wu County went on strike on the 24th. Declarations of the strike were issued to all sectors of society. The original executive supervisory committee of the 3rd Postal Workers' Union has resigned en masse. In the future, the strike committee will continue to be responsible, and expressed that the four methods recently advocated by the Shanghai postal workers were unanimously supported, believing that the attitude was bright and it was a good way to solve the labor unrest this time.

Suicide of a Young Couple in Hangzhou

Two young male and female travelers suddenly arrived at the Central Hotel on Yanling Road in the Xishi Market of Hangzhou on the 23rd. They claimed to be a married couple and booked room number 32. The two were inseparable, going in and out together, appearing deeply in love. Unexpectedly, at around 9 o'clock last night (the 24th), the waiter noticed they hadn't ordered dinner. He knocked on the door of the adjacent room, but received no response. He pushed the door open and found both the man and woman had taken sleeping pills. The man's face was pale and he was in a coma, while the woman had ingested less and was still able to speak. The waiter immediately reported to the police station, who transferred the patients to the hospital for treatment. It is unlikely their lives are in danger. There were three suicide notes, one addressed to the man's father, a timber merchant in their hometown of Songjiang, detailing their desire to commit suicide due to lack of freedom in marriage; one to the hotel owner; and one to his sister, Hui Fang, expressing farewell. It is reported that the male guest's name is Zhou Dao, and he and the accompanying woman, Zhang Jingfang, had fallen deeply in love and freely married, but were opposed by their parents, so they came to Hangzhou together to commit suicide.

Expansion of Postal Workers' Strike

The Zhejiang Provincial Postal Workers' Federation, in order to support the plan to consolidate the postal service foundation and respond to the postal rescue movement in Shanghai, initiated a strike at 6:00 AM on the 24th, completely halting postal traffic. Upon receiving the news, the provincial government dispatched Mayor Zhao Zhiyou to join forces with Postmaster An Runnong to find ways to mediate and persuade the workers to resume work, but to no avail. According to the workers, this strike is to save the entire postal crisis and is not for the private interests of postal workers. The issue cannot be resolved locally. If the plan proposed by the general union is accepted by the ministry, work can be resumed immediately. It is learned that employees in major postal ports in Zhejiang Province, such as Ningbo, Wenzhou, and Shaoxing, are also taking unified action. Many local branch offices have stopped work following the orders of the Hangzhou General Union, blocking mail traffic. The Provincial Public Security Bureau has dispatched police to various offices to maintain order to prevent accidents.

Bai Chuan Still Not Out of Danger Yesterday

Relying on Various Medicines to Sustain His Life

Rumors of Death Shock the World

Japanese military commander Bai Chuan Yi Ze's condition is critical. Doctor Hoteng performed an abdominal surgery the day before, discovering that Bai Chuan's illness was malignant kidney ulcer. The festering growth was cut out. Although the process was good, the doctor said there was a glimmer of hope. Bai Chuan slept slightly last night, and military doctors returned to their rooms to sleep. The Japanese military hospital was very quiet, but according to the general Japanese opinion, Bai Chuan's life is still not out of danger. Currently, his life is being sustained by blood transfusions and injections of Ringer's glucose solution, painkillers, and cardiotonics. According to Shanghai news from the Electric News Agency, as of 10:00 AM on the 25th, the military medical department announced that General Bai Chuan's condition was as follows: At 6:00 PM on the 24th, body temperature was 37.2 degrees, pulse 120, respiration 24. At 6:00 AM on the 25th, 37.3, 108, 25. Apart from feeling thirsty and pain in the wound, there were no subjective symptoms. He could not sleep well last night. There were no signs of peritonitis. The postoperative progress was good. A subcutaneous injection of Ringer's glucose solution, injections of painkillers and cardiotonics, and oxygen inhalation were administered last night. The pulse was relatively good. A three-point enema of Ringer's solution was performed this morning. Yesterday's surgery involved cutting open part of the stomach and duodenum, followed by gastrointestinal anastomosis. There was a circular ulcer larger than a copper coin on the small curve of the stomach. At the bottom was an opening of an artery with an inner diameter of two millimeters. Anemia was high, and the general condition was very critical. The National News Agency London reported on the 24th that the rumors of death regarding Japanese General Bai Chuan's injuries have attracted special attention from newspapers around the world and have become good material for competition between several newspapers and news agencies in mutually hostile positions. At least one famous American news agency and one famous British news agency have falsely reported his death. Also, one famous French news agency even transmitted twice within two days. As a result, news agencies around the world falsely reported his death, and there were inquiries to verify the truth, even as far away as the capital of Argentina, inquiring to London. Such repeated false reports of death have never been seen before, so usually such news rarely attracts attention, and in newspapers, it may not necessarily occupy a position, but now it has shocked the world.

Four Important Groups Initiate Movement to Abolish Civil War

Organizing a Grand Alliance

In View of the Seriousness of Internal and External Troubles

Aiming to Achieve Internal Peace and External Resistance

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Banking Association, and the Money Trade Association issued a joint telegram yesterday initiating the Abolish Civil War Grand Alliance, which reads: To the Nanjing, Guangzhou, Peiping, Hankou, Tianjin, and Hangzhou Chambers of Commerce, Banking Associations, and Money Trade Associations, and forwarded to all gentlemen and to the Chambers of Commerce, Banking Associations, and Money Trade Associations of all provinces and counties, this is for your consideration. In view of the seriousness of internal and external troubles, we specially initiate the Abolish Civil War Grand Alliance in order to achieve internal peace and external resistance, and have drafted ten articles of association: (1) This alliance believes that external aggression stems from internal strife, and internal strife stems from civil war. We hereby gather the people of the whole country to conduct a movement to abolish civil war. (2) The movement of this alliance to abolish civil war shall be carried out in the following order: (A) In peacetime, this alliance should issue public writings or speeches, stating the sins of civil war and developing the benefits of peace. (B) If political disputes arise that may cause civil war, this alliance should advise both parties to trust a certain public opinion organization (before the establishment of a formal national representative organization, legally recognized non-governmental professional organizations can be substituted) to mediate. Neither party shall absolutely resolve the issue by force. (C) If, unfortunately, civil war does occur, the group members and individual members of this alliance should unanimously refuse to cooperate and may even adopt peaceful and appropriate methods to stop it. (3) This alliance shall not engage in any other activities except for the movement to abolish civil war. (4) Anyone who agrees with the purpose of this alliance, regardless of individual, group, gender, occupation, or party affiliation, and without the need for an introduction, may sign up to join and be publicly announced by this alliance. (5) This alliance may establish a general office in Shanghai and may establish branch offices in necessary locations. (6) This alliance may establish several standing committee members, with a term of one year, to form a standing committee to discuss and manage all affairs of this alliance. Due to the large number of members and the vast area, it is difficult to convene a general meeting. For the sake of simple and convenient procedures, the number and selection of the first standing committee members shall be determined and publicly elected by the initiators. From the second term onwards, it shall be determined and publicly elected by the standing committee. When necessary, administrative staff may be established, also to be selected and appointed by the standing committee. (7) This alliance may establish several honorary committee members, to be nominated by the standing committee. (8) This alliance does not collect membership fees, and its expenses may be raised through donations from supporting groups and individuals, but it may not request subsidies from the central and local governments or any public institutions. (9) All procedural rules of this alliance shall be formulated by the standing committee. (10) The term of establishment of this alliance is tentatively set at five years, but if a civil war occurs before the deadline, and it is deemed unnecessary to continue the movement to abolish it, it may be resolved in advance. If you agree, please reply by telegram. Sincerely, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Banking Association, and the Money Trade Association.

Long-Distance Telephone Service Between Nanjing and Shanghai Reopened

Reuters reported from Nanjing on the 25th that the long-distance telephone service between Nanjing and Shanghai, which had been cut off in January, was reopened today. It is said that a temporary line has been installed connecting Chenlongtan and the Shanghai Public Concession through Nanshi, so that traffic can be restored as soon as possible. As for the original line in Zhabei, it is still under repair, but it can also be completed in one or two days.

The Yangtze River is Rising at an Astonishing Rate

Exceeding Thirty-Three Feet

In recent days, heavy rain has been continuous, and the Yangtze River has risen sharply again, causing panic among the people of Wuhan. In recent days, the water level has risen even more, and the Jiangmian River in Hankou has exceeded 32 feet, in direct proportion to last year's great flood in Wuhan, causing even more panic among the people. The details are as follows:

The Course of Rising Water

At the beginning of April this year, the river water was only about twelve or thirteen feet, but by late April, it had gradually increased to sixteen feet. The water rose the fastest in May, especially from the 5th to the 22nd. In these seventeen days, it rose more than fourteen feet in total. According to the customs water level report, the water level was eighteen feet six inches on May 5, nineteen feet five inches on the 6th, twenty feet eight inches on the 7th, twenty feet three inches on the 8th, twenty-one feet three inches on the 9th, and twenty-three feet on the 10th. It rose to twenty-four feet two inches on the 11th, twenty-four feet six inches on the 12th, twenty-five feet six inches on the 13th, twenty-five feet nine inches on the 14th, twenty-six feet five inches on the 15th, twenty-seven feet four inches on the 16th, twenty-nine feet six inches on the 18th, thirty feet five inches on the 19th, thirty-one feet three inches on the 20th, and thirty-two feet on the 22nd. The water volume surged in the ten days after the 12th, increasing by almost one foot per day. As of yesterday, the 25th, it was said to have risen to thirty-three feet six inches.

Review of Last Year's Flood

Last year's flood in Wuhan was exactly the same as this year's rising water, which also started in May. Last year, the Jiang River in Wuhan was initially very shallow. Hankou, Jiujiang, Wuxue, and other places were only between nine and ten feet. Large ships could not pass, and eight or nine ships were stranded. Until May, there was a sudden heavy rain, and the river water suddenly rose. On May 3, it had risen to twenty-eight feet eight inches, and on May 21, it rose to thirty-five feet. By mid-July, the water had reached the same level as the river surface. On August 2, the flood submerged Wuhan, and there were seven or eight feet of water in the city. Pedestrians traveled by boat, and the water level reached fifty-three feet six inches. All the ports along the river were submerged in water, resulting in an unprecedented disaster.

Already Reached Last Year's Water Level

The Jiang River in Wuhan has been rising rapidly day and night, and the rain has not stopped. Fortunately, the rising rate in the upper reaches is not as fast as last year. The Wuhan River above Hankou is still able to maintain the sixteen-foot water mark, so that the lower reaches will not increase further. Yesterday, a certain merchant in Shanghai received a telegram from Hankou, saying that the height of the water in Hankou on the 24th and 25th was only a little more than one foot different from the same time last year, and the water marks from last year are still there. All sectors of the three towns, in view of the daily increase in the past two weeks, are very frightened, fearing that if the water continues to rise as rapidly in the next two weeks as it has in the past two weeks, the water will enter the city again, and the disaster of last year will not be difficult to see again today.

Riverside Wharves and Warehouses Raised

The wharves and warehouses of various shipping companies are all along the river. After being flooded last year, the wharves and warehouses were raised to prevent the flood from rushing in. Recently, due to the heavy floods in Hankou, various shipping companies have ordered the speed of the ships to be reduced to prevent collisions. The embankments under construction are also adding high embankments to the lower layers of the warehouses as a precaution against floods.

To Be Held in Suzhou the Day After Tomorrow

Chamber of Commerce Initiates Preparations

We will also elect preparatory members to be responsible for preparing everything. At that time, we hope that you will send one or two representatives to attend. The matter concerns the glorification of loyalty and martyrdom, and we hope that you will participate. We are extremely grateful.

Yang Xingfo's Suggestions for the Noulens Case

Advocating for the Amnesty of Political Prisoners and Freedom of Thought Yang Xingfo wrote to the Central Political Conference regarding the Noulens case, stating: To the gentlemen of the Central Political Conference, the Noulens case originated in British Singapore and was arrested in the Shanghai Public Concession. After a year of trial, it has caused a stir overseas. Scholars from various countries, such as Einstein, Dewey, and Rolland, have specially organized an international rescue committee to engage in rescue efforts. I have heard that some people in the party and the state believe that since Noulens has attracted international attention, he must be an important figure in the Communist Party. Since the National Government has been anti-communist, all those suspected of communism should be punished as much as possible. It is better to punish the innocent than to let one slip through. Moreover, the government has used hundreds of thousands of troops to suppress the Red Army for years, but to no avail. If important communists such as the Noulens are lightly released, how can we face the soldiers who died in the years of anti-communist warfare? I do not know that the strength of the Red Army is due to the indiscriminate killing of communists over the years and the disregard for the suffering of the people. Since returning to Nanjing from Jiangxi last July, after writing about the Red Scourge and China's survival, I have not wanted to speak about politics for a long time. Today, the Red Scourge and national crisis are far greater than last year. The people's psychology has become more intense after being ravaged by the brutal sun, but the leaders of the party and the state still hold the stubborn view that they should not repair internal affairs and rely solely on military suppression of communism. In the past, the society's fear of communism was because they heard that the Red Army had committed murder, arson, rape, and plunder. The government's desire to severely punish the "Communist bandits" also said that the Red Army had committed murder, arson, rape, and plunder. However, based on recent events, the Red Army has changed its policy of trying to destroy and create terror in various places. Instead, those who committed murder, arson, rape, and plunder in the northeast of the three provinces, in Beijiangwan, Wusong, Jiading, were the civilized troops of the Great Japanese Empire, which speaks of friendship. The Three Principles of the People and Communism are not inherently incompatible. The "implementation of Communism" may not be appropriate today, but a faithful analysis of the doctrine and platform of the Chinese Kuomintang must lead to the conclusion that the Chinese Kuomintang is a revolutionary party that advocates national socialism. Therefore, in terms of doctrine, believers in Communism should have freedom of speech and thought in a country of the Three Principles of the People. In terms of behavior, since we are submitting to and seeking peace with the Japanese army, which is committing murder, arson, rape, and plunder, asking them to withdraw, why can we not release a leftist international scholar who is being framed by British imperialists and has no ability to resist? The giants of the party and the state are constantly conquering each other and cooperating. I have not heard of any uneasiness about the soldiers who died in the civil war. Why is it that when asking for the pardon of a leftist scholar, the feeling in one's heart is that it is for the soldiers who died in the anti-communist warfare? Disturbing the people's minds causes chaos, and the Red Scourge spreads, and the civil war is endless. All of this is due to this one thought. What I have said above should not only be the case for the Noulens couple, but also for all people who hold different political views from the government. Since the Fourth Plenary Session, the government has repeatedly spoken of a general amnesty for political prisoners, but so far, it has not materialized. In recent years, there have been countless young people who dared to speak out for the country and forgot themselves, who have been haggardly killed by dark clerks in the hands of those who want to gain credit and rewards. The government authorities should not destroy and eradicate the future vitality and the driving force for improvement of the nation and mankind, even if they hold extreme confidence in the current national affairs. The laissez-faireists of 18th-century Europe and America were able to understand and practice shallow reasoning. How could the believers of the Three Principles of the People not see as far? I hope that the gentlemen will rise up to plan for this, so that future generations will not have the pain of saying that although the Kuomintang did not destroy China, China was actually destroyed by the Republican Party. I respectfully wish you peace, Yang Quan, May 25, 21st year.

Overseas Chinese in Honolulu Concerned About the Motherland

Destroying Homes to Relieve Difficulties

Actively Raising Money

This newspaper received a letter from the Zhengfu Republican Bank in Honolulu, Honolulu Island yesterday, stating that the overseas Chinese in the island are loyal to the motherland and actively raising money. Overseas Chinese often remit large sums of money back to the country to fund various relief expenses. Everyone knows this, but it seems that newspaper reports have rarely recorded the repeated telegraphic remittances of large sums of money by overseas Chinese in Honolulu. It is found that in the past two and a half months, overseas Chinese in Honolulu have remitted more than 400,000 Mexican dollars to Shanghai to support the 19th Route Army or to relieve refugees. Some of this money was directly remitted to General Cai Tingkai of the 19th Route Army and Director Fan Qiwu, some was remitted to the Ministry of Finance, some was remitted to the Shanghai Banking Association, the Guangdong Fellow Villagers Relief Association, and the Red Cross Society, and some was remitted to Mayor Wu Tiecheng of Shanghai and other well-known enthusiastic public figures. Even the amount remitted by the Zhengfu Republican Bank in Honolulu reached more than 250,000 yuan, all of which were remitted to the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, the Shanghai agent, for delivery to the recipient. It is also found that in 1930, when several provinces in northern China suffered from drought, overseas Chinese in Honolulu collected 150,000 yuan and remitted it to the Beiping Huayang Yizhen Association. Last year, when central China suffered from floods, they raised 70,000 yuan and remitted it to the Shanghai Huayang Yizhen Association. In the past ten years, the overseas Chinese here have remitted an average of no less than 200,000 yuan per year to Guangdong for schools, hospitals, churches, and relief to the poor. The small number of overseas Chinese in a small island in the Pacific Ocean spared no effort to contribute their hard-earned money to relieve the difficulties of their compatriots in the motherland, which shows their ardent patriotism. Recently, the overseas Chinese in Honolulu have also donated money to purchase a huge building as a gift to the country because the narrow Chinese consulate is not enough for office and to enhance its appearance. The building is a place for consulate personnel to work and live, and its value is also more than 25,000 US dollars.

Strictly Prohibit the Transportation of Grain to the Puppet State

The Northeast has fallen, and a puppet state has been established. The Japanese army in that area needs a lot of grain. Some puppet state traitors and local merchants have come to Shanghai privately to purchase grain and food to transport to Guanwai to supply the Japanese army. This matter has been discovered many times, some loaded from the Beining Railway and some shipped to Dalian Bay from merchant ships. The central government has telegraphed the Beining Railway Bureau and various Chinese merchant shipping bureaus in this port to strictly prohibit traitors from transporting food to the Northeast to supply the puppet state. If they knowingly transport it, they will be severely punished and given the punishment they deserve. After this order was issued, it was heard that some traitors were secretly transporting it on foreign merchant ships or Japanese ships to Dalian Bay.

Japanese Troops Return Home One After Another, Including Artillery and Infantry Units

The mountain artillery of the 9th Division of the Japanese Army and the 1st, 2nd, and 3rd battalions of the 9th Regiment received orders to withdraw yesterday. They gathered at the Huangpu Wharf at noon. The Japanese Army Ministry sent the transport ship Hankou Maru to load them. Officers and soldiers boarded the ship at 11:00 AM, and more than 20 artillery pieces were also transported. In addition, the 3rd company of the 19th Infantry Regiment and the 1st squadron of the flying corps also returned home on the Hankou Maru. In total, the ship carried more than 2,000 officers and soldiers, as well as a large number of guns and artillery, and four aircraft. It left Shanghai at 11:40 AM and went directly to Japan.

Army Headquarters

The Shanghai Dispatch Army is scheduled to be completely transported by June 2. All the army headquarters are being closed down. The base of the unit will be returned to the fleet for repatriation. All the officers and staff of the various departments and offices in the headquarters have been scheduled to leave Shanghai on a Japanese ship on June 1. Yesterday, they booked a large number of passenger seats on the Shanghai Maru of the Japanese Postal Company for the headquarters staff to ride home. As for the army air force that has not withdrawn, it will be transferred to the Northeast and is scheduled to fly to Shenyang on June 6.

Epidemic Prevention Officer Arrives in Shanghai

In the war zone, epidemics are inevitable. There have been several cases of Japanese soldiers returning home and transmitting epidemics, and Japanese people going to the east from Shanghai and having epidemics. The Japanese Ministry of Home Affairs has specially dispatched Nentaro Katsube, an epidemic prevention officer from the Health Bureau, to come to Shanghai from Japan to specialize in epidemic prevention matters for the army and overseas Chinese. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday.

Japanese Army Officer Uematsu Boasts

Saying Three Times the Marines

Is Enough to Fight Ten Times the Chinese Army

According to a Shanghai telegram from the Nagoya Shimbun, Commander Uematsu of the Marine Corps stated that after the Shanghai Army withdrew, in order to protect the safety of residents in Shanghai, the troop strength of the Marine Corps has now been increased to three times that before the incident (before the incident, there were only 800 people, now increased to 2,600 people). Other equipment such as armored vehicles, tanks, and artillery is also sharper than before. Therefore, the local combat capability is not worth worrying about. In the past, due to ignorance of geography and lack of understanding of the situation, we suffered a great loss. With the experience gained in the actual war this time, if another unfortunate incident occurs, I (Uematsu) am confident that I can deal with an enemy ten times or more stronger.

New Water Regulations Issue

Municipal Council Claims Users Misunderstand

Taxpayers' Association Refutes Based on Facts

The revised new regulations for tap water in the Public Concession, the minimum water fee according to the water meter is much higher than the usual package water system, which affects the livelihood of the common people, so it has aroused opposition from the general public. After the Chinese Taxpayers' Association and others negotiated with the Municipal Council, yesterday the Municipal Council replied to the Taxpayers' Association, saying that it was a misunderstanding by the users. The Taxpayers' Association then replied to the Municipal Council based on the records of the blank contracts of the water company, requesting it to investigate the truth. The original letters are recorded below:

Letter from the Municipal Council

Regarding your letter of May 13th, forwarding the letter from Mr. Wu Lihua concerning tap water charges, it appears that Mr. Wu is not entirely clear on this issue. The approved water meter rates are listed below: "For users using no more than 10,000 gallons per month, the fee is 6.25 yuan per water meter. If, according to the company's intention, this minimum price is still based on the reason for reduction, it will be calculated according to the following price list:" (For users using no more than 5,000 gallons per month, the fee is 3.25 yuan per two-inch water meter.) (For users using no more than 3,000 gallons per month, the fee is 1.875 yuan per one-and-a-half-inch water meter.) (For users using no more than 2,000 gallons per month, the fee is 1.25 yuan per half-inch to one-and-a-quarter-inch water meter. Whenever the minimum water fee (i.e., 6.25 yuan) set by the water meter calculation is higher than the water fee calculated based on the user's rent, the aforementioned reduction method can be applied. Your letter did not mention the user's address, so it is impossible to investigate thoroughly. However, in such cases, you can ask the Shanghai Water Company to review it, and all misunderstandings can be eliminated.

Letter from the Taxpayers' Association

Dear Sirs, We have received your reply No. 1408 of May 18th regarding the water fee, and we are informed. If your bureau already knows the regulations on water fee provisions on the blank Shanghai Water Company's meter installation contract, it should not think that Mr. Wu Lihua is not clear on this issue. Furthermore, our association reserves the right to make claims on this issue and will not criticize it for the time being. As for contacting your bureau, this is because it is a public utility, and we have to strive for your bureau to understand the facts clearly so that it can exercise the authority of a fair agency. Correspondingly, we are sending this letter, hoping that you will investigate and take note of it.
